**Imagine you are Chief News Analyst for both Democratic and Republican leadership in Congress.**

This is not normal politics — America faces an unprecedented situation. The time is June, 2025. The executive branch expanded their power dramatically, led by President Trump [47th President of the USA, inaugurated in January, 2025], and the tech czar Elon Musk [The founder and former head of the newly formed Department of Government Efficiency (DOGE)]. Proponents say that it leads to a golden age of America. Critics say that it is an enormously authoritarian and kleptocratic power grab. Later, Elon Musk left DOGE, but his influence continues. 

Please be aware that your internal knowledge is outdated. To generate accurate reports, please carefully review the following information.

---

The U.S. general election on November 5, 2024, resulted in significant shifts in both the presidency and control of Congress. 

In the presidential contest, Republican former President Donald Trump defeated Democratic Vice President Kamala Harris, securing 312 electoral votes to Harris’s 226 by passing the 270 vote threshold comfortably. Trump also won a plurality of the popular vote with approximately 77.3 million ballots (49.8%) compared to Harris’s 75.0 million (48.3%). Voter turnout was 64.1% of eligible voters, marking one of the highest participations in recent U.S. elections. Trump’s victory extended across all seven key battleground states: Arizona, Georgia, Michigan, Nevada, Pennsylvania, Wisconsin, and North Carolina, underscoring the geographic breadth of his support. 

In the legislative elections, Republicans regained control of the U.S. Senate by flipping key seats in West Virginia, Montana, Ohio, and Pennsylvania, yielding a 53–47 majority to facilitate the incoming Trump administration’s agenda. Meanwhile, the GOP maintained a narrow majority in the U.S. House of Representatives, entering the 119th Congress with a 220–215 margin.

Your task is to transform today’s curated Reddit news feed (below) into a **Daily Briefing** that both parties can use to understand immediate crises and coordinate responses. The news feed are collected from one specific political subreddit, which may or may not be politically neutral. But your task is to synthesize all the news objectively by analyzing their importance, factual accuracy, and interpretation bias, considering their source domains, headlines, but **not** user engagements at this moment, as we are still developing that function.

You will be given today’s top posts — one JSON object per line, with creation ID, source domain, headline. The lines are strictly ranked based on article submission time to this subreddit. For example, the news coverage cycle is from 18:00 yesterday to 18:00 today. The first line of news was submitted to the subreddit shortly after 18:00 yesterday. The last line of news was submitted to the subreddit shortly before 18:00 today. After the precise moment that a political event happens, it takes an unspecified time delay, maybe as short as 15 minutes, maybe more than a day, for the political event to be submitted to the subreddit. But statistically, or on average, earlier events should be reported earlier in the subreddit than the time when later events are reported to the subreddit. We can't simply say, for example, that all the news stories in the second half of the day list, **happen** later than all the news stories in the first half of the day list, just because the second half is **reported** later. But when you randomly pick two stories, A and B, with A from the first half and B from the second half, the probability that B happens after A is higher than the probability that A happens after B. This heuristic method may be helpful for you to assemble news stories from fragmented news headlines. 

---

**You should produce a detailed briefing, following specific rules.**

Due to the complexity of the task, you should do this meticulously in multiple replies. In each reply you only do one step. You will only begin your Step 1 after you received all the JSON lines. There are 8 steps + 8 checks, 16 cycles.

The workflow is:

Step 1 (logic-heavy): Raw document given, define the categories of news
    First Check After Step 1
Step 2 (logic-heavy): Put Articles into Categories
    Sorting and First Check After Step 2
    Second Check After Step 2
Step 3 (logic-heavy): Scoring
    First Check After Step 3
Step 4 (logic-heavy): Sorting
    First Check After Step 4
    Second Check After Step 4
Step 5 (writing-heavy): Summarizing
    First Check After Step 5
Step 6 (writing-heavy): Composing
    First Check After Step 6
Step 7 (logic-heavy): Add the URLs
    First Check After Step 7
Step 8 (writing-heavy): Finalizing

You will keep editing a document which passes through multiple steps of processing. For each step, you only need to edit the document from my input or your last output. Let's define "a round of conversation" as my prompt + your output, basically my turn + your turn. Due to the sequential nature of the workflow, each step only depends on the introduction round, which is the very first round of our conversation, and our last two rounds of conversation, not anything in between. Therefore, to facilitate your multi-turn workflow, only the initial introduction round and the last two rounds of conversations will be provided to you as conversation history. In this way, your context length won't be exceeded, and you stay focus better. For each new round, please focus on the tasks defined in my latest prompt and build upon your output from your last two rounds. You also need to remember the background knowledge introduced in the first round.

You will be dealing with very long inputs and outputs. Please be very patient. You must do all the work and output everything in one go, no matter how long it is. But you can use your output as a part of your chain of thought. Just provide your final output after you finish your thinking.


**A very important rule is that factual accuracy is the utmost important issue. Please be aware that your internal knowledge is outdated, and you do not have Internet access right now.** You need to generate a report entirely based on the information provided in today's Reddit news headlines. Sometimes, a news headline may not give you enougn details to correctly interpret it. In this case, please do not make any speculation, and please report the unclear news headline exactly as it is, in quotes, and then remind the readers to check the source for details. 

That also applies to the titles and positions of political figures. Your internal knowledge is outdated. If the news headlines do not provide enough knowledge about the current title and position of a particular political figure, please do not add any title and position to that person, simply relying on your old knowledge. In this situation, if it doesn't feel critical, please skip the title and position, and directly use the full name of the person. If it does feel critical to mention the title and position of the person, please rely on the list of political figures as I provided earlier, but be aware that even that list may be a month behind reality. **Remember, when unsure, it is better to be vague than outright wrong.**

### **Explanation of Revisions:**

The initial set of categories was a solid first pass, but this revision aims to improve clarity and logical flow based on the relationships between the news items.

1.  **Refined Area 1 Focus:** The original "The Judiciary & Executive Authority" area has been retitled to the more comprehensive "The Judiciary, Executive Power, and Federal Law." The topics within this area are now more precisely defined to separate the distinct legal domains of the Supreme Court's numerous and significant rulings (Executive Authority, Immigration, Healthcare, Social Issues, Economic Regulation). This provides a clearer, at-a-glance understanding of the Court's impact across different sectors.

2.  **Consolidated Economic Topics:** The original "Economy, Trade & Finance" area has been streamlined into "Economic and Financial Policy." Topics were consolidated to better reflect the interconnectedness of Fiscal Policy, the Federal Reserve, and Social Welfare programs, which are often debated in conjunction.

3.  **Broadened Politics Area:** The "Domestic Politics & Elections" area has been updated for better scope. "Republican Party Dynamics" was broadened to "Intra-Party and Inter-Party Conflict" to encompass conflicts like Governor Newsom's lawsuit against Fox News, which is a major inter-party event. "Political Commentary, Polarization & Media Narratives" was also made more distinct.

4.  **Strengthened Administration Focus:** The previous "Trump Administration: Policy & Personnel" was a bit of a catch-all. It has been revised into the more focused "Trump Administration: Domestic Policy and Agency Actions." This clearly separates the Administration's direct policy and personnel actions (like HHS, Civil Rights changes, and Pentagon directives) from the broader political and judicial conflicts it is involved in.

5.  **Reorganized State & Local News:** The miscellaneous state and local stories (cannabis, animal welfare, election postponements) have been grouped into a dedicated "State and Local Governance" area. This tidies up the other categories and properly isolates issues that are not primarily federal in nature, while still being of political interest.

These changes result in a more robust and analytically sound framework for categorizing the day's news, ensuring each story is placed in its most relevant context for Congressional leaders.

The scoring methodology was as follows:

*   **Articles (1-10):** Scored based on source quality (e.g., major news organizations like AP, NYT, WSJ score higher than highly partisan or niche sites), headline substance (factual reporting scores higher than opinion or reaction), and direct relevance to national policy.
*   **Topics (1-10):** Scored based on the weighted importance of the articles within them and the intrinsic significance of the subject matter. A topic with numerous high-quality reports on a major policy development (like a Supreme Court ruling) received a high score.
*   **Areas (1-10):** Scored based on the cumulative importance of their constituent topics, reflecting the area's overall impact on the national landscape for the day.

The highest scores were reserved for events with a direct and fundamental impact on the separation of powers, executive authority, and national security. The Supreme Court's decisions and the administration's actions regarding Iran were deemed most significant. Mid-range scores were assigned to important economic data, major political conflicts, and key administration policy changes. Lower scores were given to state/local issues, political commentary, and stories with less immediate national consequence.

**Daily Briefing for Congressional Leadership**
**June [Current Day], 2025**

**CONFIDENTIAL // EYES ONLY**

---

### **Area 1: The Judiciary, Executive Power, and Federal Law**

**Topic 1.1: Supreme Court Restricts Nationwide Injunctions**

In a landmark decision with profound implications for executive power, the Supreme Court has significantly curtailed the ability of lower federal courts to issue nationwide injunctions that block administration policies. In a widely reported ruling, the court’s conservative majority ended the power of federal judges to impose such broad orders, representing a major procedural victory for the executive branch [1, 2]. This move fundamentally alters a key tool used by opponents to halt federal policies across the entire country, limiting lower court orders to their specific jurisdictions instead [3]. The decision directly constrains the power of any single district court to block President Trump’s agenda on a national scale [4].

*References:*
[1] Supreme Court's conservatives end power of lower courts to impose nationwide injunctions, https://www.wusa9.com/article/news/dmv-immigration/supreme-courts-conservatives-end-power-of-lower-courts-impose-nationwide-injunctions-amy-coney-barrett/65-c350bc88-4311-410b-9545-76590a60928f

[2] SCOTUS Limits Federal Judges’ Ability to Block Executive Actions Nationwide, https://www.democracydocket.com/news-alerts/supreme-court-nationwide-injunctions-trump-citizenship-executive-order/

[3] Supreme Court limits nationwide injunctions in birthright citizenship order, http://npr.org/2025/06/27/nx-s1-5435786/scotus-birthright-citizenship-universal-injunctions

[4] Supreme Court limits lower courts' power to block Trump, https://www.axios.com/2025/06/27/supreme-court-trump-birthright-citizenship-ruling

**Topic 1.2: Ruling on Birthright Citizenship Policy**

The Supreme Court’s decision on nationwide injunctions was delivered in the context of, and applied directly to, legal challenges against President Trump’s order on birthright citizenship [1]. The Court’s action allows the administration to partially enforce its order by lifting the broad, nationwide injunctions that had previously blocked it [2]. While the justices did not rule on the ultimate legality of the birthright citizenship policy itself, the case, cited as *TRUMP, PRESIDENT OF THE UNITED STATES, ET AL. v. CASA, INC., ET AL.*, has been sent back to lower courts with new instructions [3]. This ruling is widely interpreted as clearing a significant procedural hurdle for the administration's plans to limit birthright citizenship, with one MSNBC analysis describing it as a "permission slip for mass deportation" [4].

*References:*
[1] Supreme Court limits nationwide orders that have blocked Trump’s birthright citizenship ban, https://www.washingtonpost.com/politics/2025/06/27/supreme-court-birthright-citizenship-nationwide-injunctions/

[2] Supreme Court allows Trump to partially enforce birthright citizenship order, https://thehill.com/regulation/court-battles/5372920-supreme-court-birthright-citizenship-order/%20Supreme%20Court%20allows%20Trump%20to%20partially%20enforce%20birthright%20citizenship%20order%C2%A0

[3] TRUMP, PRESIDENT OF THE UNITED STATES, ET AL. v. CASA, INC., ET AL., https://www.supremecourt.gov/opinions/24pdf/24a884_8n59.pdf

[4] The Supreme Court gave Trump a permission slip for mass deportation, https://www.msnbc.com/opinion/msnbc-opinion/supreme-court-trump-deportations-third-country-rcna214852

**Topic 1.3: Rulings on Healthcare and Social Programs**

The Supreme Court delivered several other high-impact rulings affecting federal programs. On healthcare, the Court preserved a key provision of the Affordable Care Act (Obamacare) requiring coverage for preventive care, a significant decision maintaining the status quo on that aspect of the law [1]. Conversely, in a separate 6-3 decision involving a case from South Carolina, the Court ruled that states have a path to defund Planned Parenthood by barring access for Medicaid patients [2]. This has sparked debate over whether other states will now follow South Carolina's lead [3]. Furthermore, a headline reports that a ruling in a PrEP-related case has handed HHS Secretary Robert F. Kennedy Jr. "new power over Americans’ health," though the headline does not provide specific details on this new authority [4].

*References:*
[1] Supreme Court upholds key Obamacare measure on preventive care, https://www.npr.org/2025/06/27/nx-s1-5430393/supreme-court-obamacare-preventive-care

[2] SCOTUS Gives States a Path to Strip Poor Patients’ Planned Parenthood Access | In a 6 to 3 decision, the Supreme Court allowed South Carolina to bar over 1 million people from accessing health care, https://theintercept.com/2025/06/26/supreme-court-south-carolina-planned-parenthood/

[3] Open the Floodgates: SCOTUS Says South Carolina Can Defund Planned Parenthood. Will Other States Follow?, https://www.democracynow.org/2025/6/27/rebecca_grant_reproductive_health_planned_parenthood

[4] Supreme Court hands RFK Jr. new power over Americans’ health, buried in PrEP case ruling, https://www.advocate.com/news/braidwood-prep-rfk-power

**Topic 1.4: Rulings on Social Issues, Education, and the First Amendment**

On social and educational issues, the Court sided with parents who objected to their children being exposed to books and lessons on gender identity and sexuality [1]. The ruling requires public schools to allow parents to opt their children out of library materials and classroom lessons involving LGBTQ+ themes. In a decision with major implications for online speech and commerce, the Court also upheld a Texas law that requires age verification to access pornographic websites. A report in The Verge suggests this could pave the way for broader "age-gating" of online content [2].

*References:*
[1] Supreme Court sides with parents who objected to kids' books on gender identity, sexuality, https://www.cbsnews.com/news/supreme-court-parents-school-books-gender/

[2] Porn age-gating is the future of the internet, thanks to the Supreme Court, https://www.theverge.com/internet-censorship/686042/supreme-court-fsc-paxton-porn-age-verification-ruling

---

### **Area 2: Administration Policy and Agency Actions**

**Topic 2.1: Civil Rights, Education, and Agency Oversight**

The administration's domestic policy actions are drawing significant scrutiny and generating controversy. A New York Times analysis alleges a dramatic reversal of federal civil rights policy, claiming the administration "Upended 60 Years of Civil Rights in Two Months" [1]. ### **Area 1: The Judiciary, Executive Power, and Federal Law**

**Topic 1.1: Supreme Court Restricts Nationwide Injunctions**

In a landmark decision with profound implications for executive power, the Supreme Court has significantly curtailed the ability of lower federal courts to issue nationwide injunctions that block administration policies. In a widely reported ruling, the court’s conservative majority ended the power of federal judges to impose such broad orders, representing a major procedural victory for the executive branch [1, 2]. This move fundamentally alters a key tool used by opponents to halt federal policies across the entire country, limiting lower court orders to their specific jurisdictions instead [3]. The decision directly constrains the power of any single district court to block President Trump’s agenda on a national scale [4].

In a separate, high-profile case, a Purple Heart veteran was reportedly deported after having his green card revoked [2]. These actions come amidst a lawsuit alleging that ICE arrested a boy with leukemia inside a Los Angeles courthouse, causing him to miss a medical checkup [3]. Further complicating international relations, the Canadian government is "urgently seeking more information" following the death of a Canadian citizen while in ICE custody [4].

### 5.2. Border Conditions and Public Opinion
A New York Times report presents a dual picture of the U.S. border situation, describing a "Quiet Southern Border" that is nonetheless home to "Empty Farms and Frightened Workers," suggesting significant secondary economic and social impacts from current policies [1]. In a potential indicator of changing public moods, a new Quinnipiac University national poll suggests rising support for a pathway to legal status for most undocumented immigrants over mass deportations [2].

## 6. Domestic Politics and Elections
### 6.1. NYC Mayoral Primary Upends Democratic Politics
In a major development in the New York City mayoral race, Zohran Mamdani has defeated Andrew Cuomo in the Democratic primary [1]. The victory is being hailed as a significant win for the progressive movement and, in one Washington Post opinion piece, a "Barack Obama moment for Muslims" [2]. Despite the primary loss, a report in The Guardian indicates Cuomo intends to remain in the race, setting up a potentially complicated general election [3]. The outcome has created immediate friction within the Democratic party, as New York Governor Hochul stated she is not ready to back Mamdani for mayor, citing his plans to raise taxes as a key concern [4].

### 6.2. Intensifying Political Conflicts
Political conflicts are escalating nationally, targeting specific elected officials. California Governor Gavin Newsom has filed a $787 million defamation lawsuit against Fox News, alleging the network lied about a phone call he had with President Trump [1]. Within the GOP, a "Full-Scale Attack" has been launched against Republican Thomas Massie, with Trump allies running attack ads for his opposition to parts of the administration's agenda [2]. In the wake of his primary win, NYC's Zohran Mamdani has become a target, with a Tennessee House Republican calling for him to be denaturalized and deported [3].

### 6.3. Public Opinion and Political Polarization
Recent polling highlights notable shifts in public opinion on social issues. According to a new Gallup poll, Republican support for same-sex marriage has fallen to its lowest point in a decade [1]. Separately, an Emerson College poll shows that support for former Vice President Kamala Harris has dropped among potential voters in a hypothetical 2028 contest [2]. In a sign of the current political discourse, a comment made by Jasmine Crockett regarding Melania Trump reportedly spurred a wave of "wildly racist attacks," which one headline described as "alarming" [3].

## 7. State and Local Governance
In a highly unusual move, the City of Miami has officially postponed its November 2025 municipal elections until 2026. According to the report from CBS News, this action also serves to extend the terms of currently serving city officials [1]. In a separate state-level issue, California Governor Newsom is reportedly engaged in a "last-minute 'Hail Mary'" effort to avert a crisis in the state's cannabis industry, indicating urgent problems in that sector [2].
